{"parentUuid":"7bfe8664-9be3-4cbf-8f7f-bf8ee2baca63","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"605f76b4-5db4-4136-ace5-2629eb95aeb8","agentId":"a59146e5a990e80cf","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01FF2CGqxRtd6RAjhEg5f38H","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# PROVISIONAL PATENT APPLICATION SPECIFICATION\n2\t\n3\t## DRAFT — FOR ATTORNEY REVIEW ONLY\n4\t\n5\t> **Legal Disclaimer**: This specification was prepared by the inventor with AI assistance\n6\t> (Claude, Anthropic). It requires review by a registered patent attorney or agent before\n7\t> filing with the United States Patent and Trademark Office. This document does not\n8\t> constitute legal advice. Claude is not a lawyer.\n9\t\n10\t> **Filing Target**: Mid-2026 as provisional application (~$320 micro-entity fee)\n11\t\n12\t> **Prior Art Disclosure Date**: February 17, 2026 (public repository at\n13\t> `github.com/lonniev/thebrain-mcp` with GPG-signed tag `v1.0.0-prior-art` dated\n14\t> February 16, 2026)\n15\t\n16\t---\n17\t\n18\t## Title of the Invention\n19\t\n20\t**System and Method for Pre-Funded Balance Monetization of Tool-Based APIs\n21\twith Composable Constraint Pricing, Hierarchical Trust Chains,\n22\tCryptographic Identity, and Network Governance**\n23\t\n24\t---\n25\t\n26\t## Cross-Reference to Related Applications\n27\t\n28\tNone. This is the initial provisional filing.\n29\t\n30\t---\n31\t\n32\t## Field of the Invention\n33\t\n34\tThe present invention relates generally to methods and systems for monetizing\n35\tapplication programming interfaces (APIs), and more particularly to a system for\n36\tmonetizing tool-based API services through pre-funded credit balances settled via\n37\tcryptocurrency micropayment networks, with composable pricing constraints, hierarchical\n38\tmulti-party revenue distribution, decentralized cryptographic identity, and community\n39\tgovernance mechanisms.\n40\t\n41\t---\n42\t\n43\t## Background of the Invention\n44\t\n45\t### The Problem of API Monetization\n46\t\n47\tApplication programming interfaces (APIs) are the primary mechanism through which\n48\tsoftware systems exchange data and invoke functionality. The emergence of AI agent\n49\tframeworks — particularly the Model Context Protocol (MCP) specification for connecting\n50\tAI assistants to external tools — has created a new class of API consumer: autonomous\n51\tsoftware agents that invoke dozens or hundreds of tool calls per session without human\n52\tintervention at each step.\n53\t\n54\tTraditional API monetization approaches fall into three categories, each with\n55\tsignificant limitations in the AI agent context:\n56\t\n57\t**Subscription models** require the API consumer to commit to recurring payments\n58\tregardless of actual usage. This \"pestering\" of the customer — demanding payment\n59\tdecisions before value is received — creates friction that discourages adoption and\n60\tpenalizes intermittent users. Subscription management overhead (billing cycles,\n61\tplan tiers, overage charges, cancellation flows) consumes engineering resources\n62\tunrelated to the core service.\n63\t\n64\t**Per-request payment negotiation models** (exemplified by the L402 protocol and the\n65\tx402 protocol, described below) require a payment interaction at the point of service.\n66\tWhen a client sends a request, the server responds with HTTP status 402 (Payment\n67\tRequired) along with payment instructions. The client must then construct a payment,\n68\ttransmit it, await confirmation, and resubmit the original request with proof of\n69\tpayment. This challenge-response pattern introduces latency, interrupts tool call\n70\tchains, and requires the client to maintain payment channel state alongside\n71\tapplication state.\n72\t\n73\t**Marketplace aggregation models** (exemplified by platforms such as MCPize, Apify,\n74\tand Masumi Network) interpose a centralized marketplace between API providers and\n75\tconsumers. The marketplace handles billing, typically through conventional payment\n76\tprocessors (Stripe, credit card networks). These platforms extract significant\n77\trevenue shares (15% or more), require providers to conform to marketplace terms,\n78\tand introduce single points of failure. None provide the provider with direct\n79\tcontrol over pricing policy or customer relationships.\n80\t\n81\t### Prior Art\n82\t\n83\t#### L402 Protocol (Lightning Labs, 2020)\n84\t\n85\tThe L402 protocol (originally named LSAT) was published by Lightning Labs in March\n86\t2020. It defines a mechanism for HTTP-native API payments using the Lightning Network.\n87\tWhen a server receives an unauthenticated request, it returns HTTP 402 with a\n88\t`WWW-Authenticate` header containing a Lightning invoice and a macaroon (a\n89\tbearer credential with attenuable caveats). The client pays the invoice, receives a\n90\tpreimage, and combines the preimage with the macaroon to form an L402 token that\n91\tauthenticates subsequent requests.\n92\t\n93\tL402 is implemented through Aperture, a reverse proxy that intercepts requests,\n94\tverifies L402 tokens, and forwards authenticated requests to the upstream service.\n95\t\n96\tL402 limitations relevant to the present invention:\n97\t\n98\t- Every request that lacks a valid token triggers a payment negotiation cycle\n99\t- No mechanism for pre-funding a balance that covers multiple future requests\n100\t- Pricing rules are configured ad hoc in the reverse proxy; no composable\n101\t  constraint system exists\n102\t- Single-party architecture with no multi-layer revenue distribution\n103\t- Identity is bound to macaroons, not to a portable cryptographic keypair\n104\t- No community governance or network coordination mechanism\n105\t\n106\tThe L402 specification mentions \"top-up\" functionality in passing but does not\n107\tdefine a pre-funded balance architecture. It mentions \"surge pricing\" as a\n108\tpossibility but provides no mechanism for implementing it.\n109\t\n110\t#### x402 Protocol (Coinbase, 2025)\n111\t\n112\tThe x402 protocol was launched by Coinbase in late 2025, with a partnership\n113\tannounced with Cloudflare in December 2025 for integration into Cloudflare's\n114\tinfrastructure. x402 defines a stablecoin-based (USDC) payment mechanism embedded\n115\tin HTTP headers. The server responds with 402 and a JSON payment requirements\n116\tobject; the client constructs a payment payload, signs it with a wallet key, and\n117\tincludes it in a `PAYMENT-SIGNATURE` header on the retry request. A \"facilitator\"\n118\tservice (hosted by Coinbase) verifies the signature and settles the payment on-chain.\n119\t\n120\tx402 limitations relevant to the present invention:\n121\t\n122\t- Same challenge-response pattern as L402 — no pre-funded balance\n123\t- Two payment \"schemes\" only: \"exact\" (fixed price) and \"upto\" (variable with ceiling);\n124\t  no composable constraint pipeline\n125\t- Relies on a centralized Facilitator service operated by Coinbase\n126\t- Identity is a blockchain wallet address, not a portable network identity\n127\t- No hierarchical trust chain or revenue distribution mechanism\n128\t- No governance layer — Coinbase controls the Facilitator and the Foundation\n129\t- Uses stablecoins (USDC) pegged to fiat currency, not native cryptocurrency\n130\t\n131\t#### MCP Monetization Platforms (2025-2026)\n132\t\n133\tSeveral platforms have emerged to monetize MCP tool services:\n134\t\n135\t- **MCPize**: Marketplace model with 85% revenue share, Stripe-based payments\n136\t- **PayMCP/Walleot**: Decorator-based tool pricing (`@price`) with multiple payment modes\n137\t  via a centralized wallet service\n138\t- **Masumi Network**: Blockchain-based (Cardano-adjacent) payment integration\n139\t- **Moesif**: Traditional API analytics and billing wrapping Stripe/Chargebee/Zuora\n140\t- **Apify**: MCP server marketplace with conventional payment rails\n141\t\n142\tNone of these platforms use the Lightning Network for settlement. None implement\n143\ta pre-funded credit balance model. None have composable constraint-based pricing.\n144\tNone have hierarchical trust chains with royalty distribution. None use\n145\tdecentralized cryptographic identity. None have community governance mechanisms.\n146\t\n147\t### Unmet Need\n148\t\n149\tThere exists a need for an API monetization system that:\n150\t\n151\t1. Eliminates per-request payment negotiation by allowing consumers to pre-fund\n152\t   a credit balance from which individual tool invocations are deducted\n153\t2. Provides API operators with a composable, programmable pricing policy engine\n154\t   rather than ad hoc price configurations\n155\t3. Supports multi-party revenue distribution through a hierarchical trust chain\n156\t   where each layer uses the same protocol, enabling franchise-like scaling\n157\t4. Uses portable, decentralized cryptographic identity that requires no\n158\t   personally identifiable information, email addresses, passwords, or OAuth tokens\n159\t5. Provides community governance mechanisms that make the network's economic value\n160\t   reside in participation rather than in proprietary code\n161\t6. Assists API operators in designing pricing policies through AI-guided structured\n162\t   interviews, with schema-aware validation, multi-provider adversarial review, and\n163\t   cryptographically authenticated deployment to live endpoints\n164\t\n165\t---\n166\t\n167\t## Summary of the Invention\n168\t\n169\tThe present invention provides an integrated system and method for monetizing\n170\ttool-based APIs through six interconnected architectural components:\n171\t\n172\t**First**, a pre-funded balance monetization system in which API consumers purchase\n173\tcredit units (\"api_sats\") via Lightning Network micropayments, and individual tool\n174\tinvocations deduct from that balance according to per-tool pricing rules, eliminating\n175\tper-request payment negotiation entirely.\n176\t\n177\t**Second**, a composable constraint engine that evaluates a pipeline of pricing\n178\tconstraints on each tool invocation — including temporal windows, finite supply caps,\n179\tperiodic refresh limits, congestion-based surge pricing, ad valorem pricing proportional\n180\tto response value, and promotional modifiers — to produce a final deduction amount.\n181\tThe constraint engine supports runtime-configurable pricing models: named bundles of\n182\tper-tool prices and constraint pipelines that are persisted in a database, activated\n183\tatomically (at most one active per operator), resolved at tool-call time through a\n184\tTTL-cached resolver, and subject to graceful degradation on database failure.\n185\t\n186\t**Third**, a hierarchical trust chain with self-similar royalty distribution, in which\n187\tan Authority certifies purchase orders for downstream Operators using cryptographic\n188\tsignatures, and each layer in the hierarchy implements the same protocol pattern. An\n189\tAuthority is structurally an Operator whose customers happen to be other Operators.\n190\tRevenue flows through the chain via certification fees. A configuration-time fee floor\n191\tinvariant ensures economic viability: each non-Prime Authority's local fee rate must\n192\tbe greater than or equal to its upstream Authority's fee rate, preventing configurations\n193\tin which an Authority would lose money on every certification. The chain also\n194\taccommodates Advocates — community utility services that provide shared infrastructure\n195\t(such as OAuth2 callback collection) without monetization, discoverable by peer\n196\tservices through registry-based service resolution. The Authority provisions each\n197\tOperator's persistence layer as an isolated database schema, and the Operator encrypts\n198\tall stored data with a key derived from its own private key — ensuring that neither the\n199\tAuthority, the infrastructure provider, nor any other Operator can read another\n200\tOperator's data. A bootstrap protocol enables an Operator to discover its full"}]},"uuid":"3ae1ccf0-949c-4740-ad33-db0e42268326","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:21:33.651Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"7bfe8664-9be3-4cbf-8f7f-bf8ee2baca63","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

DEV Community\",\"url\":\"https://dev.to/umangbuilds/x402-protocol-complete-guide-to-http-native-micropayments-2ne1\"},{\"title\":\"bitcoin | Bitcoin In Plain English\",\"url\":\"http://www.bitcoininplainenglish.com/wordpress/?cat=7\"},{\"title\":\"BIP70 payment protocol | Bitcoin Optech\",\"url\":\"https://bitcoinops.org/en/topics/bip70-payment-protocol/\"},{\"title\":\"BitPay, Payment Protocol (BIP-70), and Our Users' Bitcoin Payment Experience | BitPay\",\"url\":\"https://www.bitpay.com/blog/bitpay-and-payment-protocol\"},{\"title\":\"What is the Strike API?\",\"url\":\"https://strike.me/learn/what-is-the-strike-api/\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here's information about BIP-0070 Bitcoin Payment Protocol and its relationship to micropayments and API monetization:\n\n## BIP-0070 Payment Protocol Overview\n\nBIP-0070 describes a protocol for communication between a merchant and their customer, enabling both a better customer experience and better security against man-in-the-middle attacks on the payment process. The BIP was authored by Gavin Andresen and Mike Hearn, with a status of Final and created on 2013-07-29.\n\n## Key Features\n\nThe protocol supports human-readable, secure payment destinations, secure proof of payment, resistance from man-in-the-middle attacks, payment received messages so customers know immediately that the merchant has received their payment, and refund addresses automatically given to the merchant by the customer's wallet software.\n\n## Micropayments Support\n\nPrograms accepting URIs in any form must ask the user for permission before paying unless the user has explicitly disabled prompting (as might be the case for micropayments). The protocol was designed with the capability to support micropayment scenarios, though widespread adoption has been limited.\n\n## Current Status\n\nIt's important to note that the payment protocol is considered to be deprecated and will be removed in a later version of Bitcoin Core, as it has multiple security design flaws and implementation flaws in some wallets, and merchants should transition away from BIP70 to more secure options such as BIP21. Additionally, BIP70 never saw widespread adoption and almost all merchants and wallets that did once support it have either ended support or plan to end their support in the future.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"f874243a-b7e7-4684-8a97-7df45e084ba9","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:21:51.455Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"35f2ff13-8e48-464a-a12d-7cd601a87e21","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

Invoice Protocol for Lightning Payments | by Omoniyi | Coinmonks | Medium\",\"url\":\"https://medium.com/coinmonks/bolt-11-invoicing-cfe178abb17c\"},{\"title\":\"bolts/11-payment-encoding.md at master · lightning/bolts\",\"url\":\"https://github.com/lightning/bolts/blob/master/11-payment-encoding.md\"},{\"title\":\"GitHub - alexbosworth/invoices: Library for parsing Lightning Network BOLT11 payment requests and encoding invoices into requests\",\"url\":\"https://github.com/alexbosworth/invoices\"},{\"title\":\"Understanding Lightning Invoices | Builder's Guide\",\"url\":\"https://docs.lightning.engineering/the-lightning-network/payment-lifecycle/understanding-lightning-invoices\"},{\"title\":\"The Lightning Invoice\",\"url\":\"https://www.bolt11.org/\"},{\"title\":\"GitHub - bitcoinjs/bolt11: A library for encoding and decoding lightning network payment requests as defined in BOLT #11. · GitHub\",\"url\":\"https://github.com/bitcoinjs/bolt11\"},{\"title\":\"15. Lightning Payment Requests - Mastering the Lightning Network [Book]\",\"url\":\"https://www.oreilly.com/library/view/mastering-the-lightning/9781492054856/ch15.html\"},{\"title\":\"BOLT 11: How to Pay People on Lightning\",\"url\":\"https://simplelightning.com/bolt-11-how-to-pay-people-with-lightning.html\"},{\"title\":\"Decoder for Lightning Payment Requests\",\"url\":\"https://lndecode.com/\"},{\"title\":\"Receiving Payments | Builder's Guide\",\"url\":\"https://docs.lightning.engineering/lightning-network-tools/lnd/receiving\"}]\n\nI've performed a web search for information about BOLT-11 Lightning Network invoices, pre-funded payment channels, and API access. Here are the key findings:\n\n## BOLT-11 Overview\n\nLightning invoices are defined by the BOLT 11 standard, where BOLT stands for 'Basis of Lightning Technology' and covers all Lightning Network specifications. The BOLTs are the documents that define the protocol specification for all Lightning implementations to communicate and interact.\n\n## Invoice Format and Structure\n\nThe QR-code-friendly format for communicating the information required to complete a payment from receiver to sender is described in BOLT #11: Invoice Protocol for Lightning Payments. The format for a Lightning invoice uses bech32 encoding, which is already used for Bitcoin Segregated Witness.\n\n## Invoice Components\n\nThis invoice is constructed by the receiver and contains information such as the amount, unit of payment, node of the receiver, and so on. Defined tags are optional fields for adding a payment hash, invoice description, expiry time, public key of the payee node, a fallback bitcoin \"onchain\" address, extra routing information for routing to an unannounced channel, payment metadata, a payment secret to prevent probing by other nodes, and more.\n\n## API Access for Payment Management\n\nThe AddInvoice endpoint adds an invoice to your node, and returns the add_index and a payment request for the invoice. The payment request encodes all of the information that sending nodes need to pay your node, and can be encoded into QR codes. The SubscribeInvoices endpoint provides a stream of updates for invoices, informing you about newly added invoices and sending notifications when they are settled, and supports historical streams.\n\nThe search results provide information about BOLT-11 invoice standards and some basic API endpoints but don't contain detailed documentation on pre-funded payment channels specifically.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"2a98da63-2bd3-457f-a45b-e44133793141","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:21:51.724Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"78b2a29f-9b71-405a-8783-c8ec1d1ac0bb","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

A kind 27235 event (in reference to RFC 7235) is used.\n\nThe u tag MUST be exactly the same as the absolute request URL (including query parameters), and the method tag MUST be the same HTTP method used for the requested resource.\n\n## NIP-57: Lightning Zaps\n\nNIP-57 defines two new event types for recording lightning payments between users. Kind 9734 is a zap request, representing a payer's request to a recipient's lightning wallet for an invoice, and kind 9735 is a zap receipt, representing the confirmation by the recipient's lightning wallet that the invoice has been paid. Having lightning receipts on nostr allows clients to display lightning payments from entities on the network, which can be used for fun or for spam deterrence.\n\n## Integration for Payment Gating\n\nThe search results indicate there is emerging work on integrating NIP-98 with NIP-57 for payment gating purposes. An extension to NIP-98 allows HTTP authorization using a base64 encoded event header, and there are proposals to combine these protocols for implementing payment-required access flows where users can authenticate via Nostr and complete payments through Lightning zaps.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"b51ca739-8abb-4f75-964a-77ac840491fb","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:21:52.959Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e2e900fb-1fad-4464-8d49-0dafc51c7bc9","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

This shift enables true economic composability where an agent can compare multiple APIs in real time, select based on price or latency, and settle per request.\n\n## Cryptocurrency Micropayments for APIs\n\nThe x402 protocol has emerged as a solution for API micropayments using blockchain. API calls can be priced at fractions of a cent — true micropayments, which are impractical with credit card processing fees that usually start at $0.30 per transaction. With stablecoins, sub-second settlement, no chargebacks, and blockchains that actually scale, x402 wires these properties into the internet's request-response loop as an open standard that lets any service charge for API or content access over HTTP without traditional accounts, sessions, or credentials.\n\n## Dynamic Pricing & Surge Pricing\n\nProviders can dynamically price endpoints, and services can compete at the level of execution rather than contract negotiation. called LSAT) and its pay-per-call implementation with Lightning Network API access tokens:\n\n## Overview\n\nL402 is an open protocol for paying for and authenticating access to APIs and services over the internet using the Lightning Network, developed by Lightning Labs, bringing to life the long-dormant HTTP 402 Payment Required status code by combining macaroons (cryptographic bearer credentials) with Lightning Network micropayments.\n\n## Pay-Per-Call Implementation\n\nInstead of choosing between free tiers and monthly subscriptions, users pay for exactly what they use, with a single API call costing fractions of a cent. L402 (formerly LSAT) enables APIs to charge per-request using Lightning Network invoices.\n\n## Authentication Flow\n\nA client requests a paid resource from a server, the server responds with 402 Payment Required, including an authentication macaroon and a Lightning invoice in the WWW-Authenticate header, the client pays the invoice over Lightning, receiving a payment preimage as proof of payment, the client re-sends the request with the macaroon and preimage in the Authorization header, and the server verifies the credential and serves the resource, with the macaroon cryptographically committing to the payment hash of the invoice.\n\n## Access Token Details\n\nLightning API keys (L402) are Macaroons that include a payment hash, and for the L402 to be valid, it must be presented together with the preimage corresponding to the payment hash. Once a token is obtained, it can be cached and reused for subsequent requests to the same service until it expires or is revoked, with an agent paying once per endpoint, not once per request.\n\n## Key Features\n\nMacaroons support attenuation: a credential holder can create a weaker version of their credential to share with others, restricting access to specific services, capabilities, or usage limits. The endpoint is able to verify that the token is valid, and that the payment is made, without access to the payment database through stateless verification.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"785a01dd-019e-4090-8bf3-80cd8b0fd84b","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:21:54.143Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"66df0316-a059-4bd2-b876-38fdbac1bf88","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

L402 (formerly LSAT) enables APIs to charge per-request using Lightning Network invoices.\n\n## Pay-Per-Call Functionality\n\nInstead of choosing between free tiers and monthly subscriptions, users pay for exactly what they use, with a single API call costing fractions of a cent. By leveraging L402s, a service or business is able to offer a new tier of paid APIs that sits between free and subscription: metered, with no login, email or passwords required.\n\n## Constraint-Based Pricing\n\nMultiple constraints may be present in an L402, but each constraint needs to be more restrictive than the previous, with examples including allowing users to access services only up to a certain monthly limit. For dynamic pricing, Aperture can be configured to connect to a separate service over gRPC, which allows for resources to be priced in fiat currency, selling a large repository of items each with their own pricing, or adjusting prices based on demand.\n\nThe search results primarily contain documentation and technical specifications from Lightning Labs rather than specific lightning-dev mailing list discussions on these topics.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"fa0faafb-369d-4106-8f8a-dbf65afccb6d","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:22:06.825Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"aeca46f2-f073-4689-ac92-1578042fbd87","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

However, NIP-44 is the newer, more secure encryption standard for Nostr, replacing NIP-04, providing better security properties and supporting additional features.\n\nNIP-44 encryption and NIP-59 seals and gift wraps define an encrypted chat scheme, with the encryption algorithm using the latest version of NIP-44. The initial version of Nostr Wallet Connect (NWC) used NIP-04 for encryption which has been deprecated and replaced by NIP-44, with NIP-44 always being preferred for encryption.\n\n## Identity Verification\n\nNIP-05 is a verification system that links your Nostr identity to a domain name, creating human-readable addresses like name@domain.com instead of long npubs, proving you control both the Nostr account and the domain.\n\nThe Nostr WoT Extension is an all-in-one browser extension that acts as your Nostr identity provider (NIP-07 signer), Lightning wallet, and Web of Trust engine, managing your keys in an encrypted vault and signing events for any Nostr client.\n\n## Payment Systems\n\nNIP-47 describes a way for clients to access a remote lightning wallet through a standardized protocol, which custodians may implement, or users may run a bridge that bridges their wallet/node and the Nostr Wallet Connect protocol. Fundamentally NWC is communication between a client and wallet service by means of E2E-encrypted direct messages over a nostr relay, where the relay knows the kinds and tags of notes, but not the content of the encrypted payloads, and the user's identity key is not used to avoid linking payment activity to the user.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"8a65ce31-4dba-48ea-b967-93e8d6b17f35","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:22:07.765Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"68aadd44-f250-4d1d-a003-d326f6cd25c6","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

Features include:\n- Client deposits funds into escrow contract\n- Per-request latency in \"low double-digit milliseconds\"\n- Per-request costs as low as $0.0001\n- Net settlement occurs on-chain periodically\n\n## Supported Payment Methods\n- Tempo (stablecoins: USDC, USDT)\n- Stripe (card payments)\n- Bitcoin Lightning\n- Solana (SOL and SPL tokens)\n\n## MCP Integration\n\"MPP includes a dedicated MCP transport binding that maps the Challenge-Credential-Receipt flow directly onto the Model Context Protocol,\" enabling agents to discover and pay for tool calls autonomously.\n\n## Production Adoption\n- **Browserbase**: Agents pay per session for headless browser access\n- **Parallel Web Systems**: Per-API-call payment for web access\n- **PostalForm**: Agents pay to print and send physical mail\n\n## Author & Publication\nTheo Vasilis, Content Production Lead at Apify | Published: April 9, 2026"}]},"uuid":"745932fa-4e7a-4f7e-b666-dfe8cab94987","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:22:33.144Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"609eb434-71ea-4c39-a774-c1182cf110d1","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

The Machine Payments Protocol (MPP) is an open standard, internet-native way for agents to pay—co-authored by Tempo and Stripe.\n\n## Pre-funded Session Escrow\n\nThe agent deposits funds into an escrow contract upfront, opens the connection, and issues vouchers for subsequent requests. The server accumulates vouchers and submits the final one onchain in one transaction, collects what it's owed, and returns any leftover deposit. An MPP session lets an agent deposit funds into an escrow contract once, then make thousands of subsequent micropayment requests using signed vouchers, without hitting the blockchain on every call.\n\n## Composable Pricing\n\nA flexible core allows advanced flows like disputes or additional primitives like identity to be gradually introduced. Additionally, MPP is payment-method agnostic. A single endpoint can accept stablecoins (Tempo), credit cards (Stripe), or Bitcoin (Lightning).\n\n## Performance Benefits\n\nPayments as small as $0.0001 per request become practical because thousands of micro-interactions batch-settle into a single on-chain transaction when the session ends. The key win: Billing can happen at the same speed as the service itself.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"f44f4d99-0b3f-4db1-8616-2ead679ca710","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:22:46.155Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"dbb35c9c-2443-4ade-a38c-a057592dab6e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

HTTP 402, realized. · GitHub\",\"url\":\"https://github.com/lightninglabs/l402\"},{\"title\":\"docs.lightning.engineering/the-lightning-network/l402/l402.md at master · lightninglabs/docs.lightning.engineering\",\"url\":\"https://github.com/lightninglabs/docs.lightning.engineering/blob/master/the-lightning-network/l402/l402.md\"},{\"title\":\"What Is The Lightning HTTP 402 Protocol, And Why Is It Important? | Nasdaq\",\"url\":\"https://www.nasdaq.com/articles/what-is-the-lightning-http-402-protocol-and-why-is-it-important\"},{\"title\":\"L402 - the Builder's Guide to the LND Galaxy! - Lightning Labs\",\"url\":\"https://docs.lightning.engineering/the-lightning-network/l402/l402\"},{\"title\":\"blips/blip-0026.md at 697ae354c205f1aacc450e72067c92a7f2467321 · Roasbeef/blips\",\"url\":\"https://github.com/Roasbeef/blips/blob/697ae354c205f1aacc450e72067c92a7f2467321/blip-0026.md\"}]\n\nI found comprehensive information about L402, macaroons, caveats, constraints, composable attenuation, and pricing. Here's what the search revealed:\n\n## L402 Protocol Overview\n\nL402 is an open protocol for paying for and authenticating access to APIs and services over the internet using the Lightning Network, developed by Lightning Labs by combining macaroons (cryptographic bearer credentials) with Lightning Network micropayments.\n\n## Macaroons and Caveats\n\nMacaroons have three basic components: a public identifier that maps to a root key, a list of caveats (which is how attenuation is achieved), and a signature. To further amend or restrict Macaroons, a \"caveat\" is added, which is a further restriction or attribute of a Macaroon.\n\n## Composable Attenuation\n\nAttenuation means a macaroon holder can add restrictions to an existing credential without contacting the issuer. For instance, a parent agent can take a macaroon and append caveats (conditions that restrict the token's use) like spending caps, service restrictions, or time-based expiration. The resulting restricted credential is cryptographically valid, carries tighter permissions, and requires no round trip to the server.\n\n## Constraints\n\nEach service capability can be further constrained. This is recorded as a separate caveat beginning with the service capability. Similar to capabilities, multiple constraints may be present in a L402, but each constraint needs to be more restrictive than the previous.\n\n## Pricing Integration\n\nThe client pays the invoice over Lightning, receiving a payment preimage as proof of payment. The macaroon cryptographically commits to the payment hash of the invoice, so the server can verify payment using only the macaroon and preimage.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"a315ecdc-55c4-43b7-8b67-2f2eb637d79c","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:22:48.326Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"734db32f-38c9-456c-9201-aa29a4e59d06","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

NWC allows for sustained interaction between bitcoin lightning wallets and apps. Once an app connection is created, the app can request payments through a Nostr relay.\n\n## How It Works\n\nFundamentally NWC is communication between a client and wallet service by the means of E2E-encrypted direct messages over a nostr relay. The relay knows the kinds and tags of notes, but not the content of the encrypted payloads.\n\n## API Methods\n\nThe Nostr Wallet Connect (NIP-47) extension methods include: pay_keysend, make_invoice, lookup_invoice, list_transactions, get_balance, get_info which can be used by developers to make awesome apps powered by NWC.\n\n## Payment Gating & Spending Limits\n\nConnection parameters support spending controls: max_amount (optional) maximum amount in sats that can be sent per renewal period · budget_renewal (optional) reset the budget at the end of the given budget renewal. Can be never (default), daily, weekly, monthly, yearly.\n\n## Pre-Funded Balance Example\n\nOne example of pre-funded balance in practice is shown in NUTbits: On failover, your spendable balance is whatever was pre-funded on the new active mint.\n\nThe search results show various implementations supporting scoped permissions and spending limits for controlling payment gating through NWC connections.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"910ffc88-51cf-4341-ab4c-581171ae42e5","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:22:49.236Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"3fffdb6d-8c1d-4f32-aae2-0ce2fc6e465e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

It supports multiple payment providers and integrates seamlessly with MCP's tool/resource interface.\n\n## Pricing Decorator\n\nPayMCP includes a `@price` decorator that allows you to add payment gating to tools by specifying the amount and currency. For example, you can use `@price(0.60, \"USD\")` to set a tool's cost.\n\n## Payment Modes\n\nPayMCP's TWO_STEP mode works by: first call invoked without payment_id returns a payment_url + payment_id and instructs a retry after payment; second call invoked with the returned payment_id verifies payment server-side and, if paid, executes the original tool logic.\n\nPayMCP includes native support for the x402 payment protocol and a dedicated Mode.X402 for clients capable of automatic on-chain payments.\n\n## Walleot Integration\n\nWith PayMCP and Walleot, you can keep your MCP server exactly as it is and simply add payments when needed.\n\n## Lightning Payment Alternatives\n\nWhile PayMCP itself primarily uses traditional payment providers, Alby released PaidMCP, an easy to use SDK for creating paid Model Context Protocol (MCP) servers, built entirely on open protocols, allowing developers to expose their services to AI assistants and charge for their use. Each resource request triggers a fresh payment flow: server issues invoice → client pays → client gains access. It states: *\"Caveats can encode service access, capabilities, expiration, volume limits, and other constraints.\"* However, the protocol specification does not define concrete caveat implementations—it defers to the macaroon technical specification for details.\n\nIdentified caveat use cases:\n- Expiry dates\n- Usage count limits\n- Volume-based tier escalation\n- IP address binding\n- TLS certificate fingerprint restriction\n\n## 3) Hierarchical Delegation or Trust Chain\n**Limited Scope.** Macaroons support attenuation through caveats, enabling credential delegation with narrowed authority. The spec notes: *\"Each successive caveat can only narrow the macaroon's authority, never widen it.\"* However, this describes **self-attenuation** (client-side restriction) rather than server-issued hierarchical chains. No multi-tier trust hierarchy is defined.\n\n## 4) Multi-party Revenue Sharing\n**Absent.** The specification makes no mention of revenue splits, multi-party payouts, or shared settlement. {"parentUuid":"1b5a1ca8-63cb-47bf-b988-4c11e804d5fb","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"7634b207-b03e-4a42-8824-214bc80332a1","agentId":"a59146e5a990e80cf","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01DHoBBsmgMomE4c9DxXdHGo","type":"tool_result","content":"# PayMCP Payment System Analysis\n\n## 1) Payment Modes\n\nPayMCP supports **two primary modes**:\n\n- **Pay-per-request**: Individual charges per tool invocation with decorator `@price(amount=0.99, currency=\"USD\")`\n- **Subscription-gated**: Access controlled via active subscriptions using `@subscription(plan=\"price_pro_monthly\")`\n\nThe system offers seven operational modes for pay-per-request flows: AUTO, X402, TWO_STEP, RESUBMIT, ELICITATION, PROGRESS, and DYNAMIC_TOOLS. Mode.AUTO intelligently detects client capabilities and selects between x402 protocol or traditional providers.\n\n## 2) Pricing Configuration\n\nPricing is **fixed at tool registration**, not dynamic. The framework allows:\n- Static amount declaration per tool via `@price` decorator\n- Currency specification (USD examples shown)\n- No evidence of surge pricing, tiered pricing, or algorithmic adjustment\n\nThe documentation states: *\"Add `@price(...)` decorators to your MCP tools to enable pay‑per‑request billing.\"* No constraint engine or composable pricing logic is described.\n\n## 3) Identity System\n\nIdentity relies on **external authentication** (developer responsibility):\n- Extracted from `ctx.authInfo` or Bearer token Authorization headers\n- Requires JWT claims: `sub` (user ID) and `email` (provider matching)\n- *\"PayMCP does **not** validate or verify the token; it only parses it\"* to extract identity\n\nNo built-in identity management; delegated to the deploying application.\n\n## 4) Trust Chain/Certification\n\n**No trust chain or certification system is documented.** The framework integrates with established payment providers (Stripe, Adyen, PayPal, etc.) but does not implement hierarchical certification, signing chains, or provider attestation mechanisms beyond standard provider authentication.\n\n## 5) Lightning Network Support\n\n**Not mentioned.** PayMCP supports x402 protocol for USDC on Base and Solana networks, but Lightning Network integration is absent from the documentation.\n\n---\n\n**Summary**: PayMCP is a decorator-based payment orchestration layer emphasizing provider agnosticity and multiple payment flow patterns, but lacks dynamic pricing, cryptographic trust infrastructure, and Lightning support."}]},"uuid":"d1078c62-3d14-4c07-aeb2-8e819e496fa5","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:23:08.923Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"1b5a1ca8-63cb-47bf-b988-4c11e804d5fb","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

To price for each resource individually, Aperture supports dynamic pricing by connecting to a separate service over gRPC, which allows for resources to be priced in fiat currency, sell a large repository of items with their own pricing, or adjust prices based on demand.\n\nThe dynamic pricing feature means that an Aperture-aware API backend can dynamically inform the proxy what the new pricing should be for a given endpoint, so in the context of LLMs, a backend could modify the price as a function of the type of model, query length, context window, and other parameters directly related to operational costs.\n\n## Rate Limiting Constraints\n\nAperture supports optional per-endpoint rate limiting using a token bucket algorithm, with rate limits configured per service and applied based on the client's L402 token ID for authenticated requests, or IP address for unauthenticated requests. kind:7001 for Subscribe Events (published by subscribers), kind:7002 for Unsubscribe Events (published by subscribers), and kind:7003 for Subscription Payment Receipts (published by payment-verifier-pubkey).\n\n## Tier System\n\nA pubkey that wants to provide others the ability to subscribe to them can create \"tiers\" that might provide certain benefits to the supporters who subscribe to these.\n\n## Payment Verification\n\nTo verify a payment, the time between zap receipts should be equal or less than the cadence specified in the kind:7001 event, and the amount of the zap receipt should be equal or greater than the amount specified in the kind:7001 event.\n\n## Access Control Features\n\nAn r tag can be included to specify a relay where clients can find special content for this tier, and zero or more p tags can be included to specify a pubkey that is trusted by the tier creator to verify payments on their behalf.\n\nThe specification integrates with the Lightning Network's zap protocol to handle recurring payments and subscription management in the Nostr protocol.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using It enables low-fee, automated payments using stablecoins on fast blockchains like Base and Solana.\n\n## MCP Integration\n\nCloudflare is shipping features to allow developers to use x402 in MCP integrations, and agents built using Cloudflare's Agent SDK can now pay for resources with x402, and MCP servers can expose tools to be paid for via x402.\n\n## Deferred Payment Scheme\n\nA new deferred payment scheme for the x402 protocol is being proposed, specifically designed for agentic payments that don't need immediate settlement and can be handled either through traditional payment methods or stablecoins.\n\n## Adoption and Growth\n\nBy December, x402 had processed 75 million transactions worth $24 million for paid APIs and AI agents. The delegator signs this hash to authorize the delegatee's keypair.\n\n## 2) Chain of Delegation Support\nThe specification does not explicitly address multi-level delegation. It describes a single authorization tier where a delegator grants permissions to one delegatee. No mention exists regarding whether a delegatee could further delegate their authority.\n\n## 3) Conditions and Constraints\nTwo primary constraint types are supported:\n- **Kind restrictions**: `=${KIND_NUMBER}` limits event types the delegatee may sign\n- **Timestamp boundaries**: `<${TIMESTAMP}` (before) and `>${TIMESTAMP}` (after) restrict event creation windows\n\nMultiple conditions combine using `&`. Best practices recommend including both an \"after\" condition (preventing historical publication) and a \"before\" condition (preventing indefinite authorization).\n\n## 4) Hierarchical Support\nThe NIP structure supports only bilateral relationships—delegator to delegatee. Here are the key findings:\n\n## Community Governance in Cryptocurrency\n\nCrypto governance involves the participation of community members, including developers, token holders, and other stakeholders, relying on consensus mechanisms and voting systems to ensure fair and inclusive decision-making processes aligned with community interests.\n\n## Governance Models\n\nThere are typically two types of cryptocurrency governance: on-chain and off-chain. With on-chain governance, voting is conducted on-chain with rules set on-chain, meaning all nodes must approve proposed changes, and on-chain governance allows for participation from all nodes supporting the network.\n\nOff-chain governance allows miners, developers, and users to participate in the decision-making process, and this type of governance increases participation from the community and not just the nodes for a blockchain.\n\n## Open Source Integration\n\nOpen development through different layers provides transparency and invites community participation in the continuous improvement of the protocol, and as a result, the organic process of decentralized protocol design becomes stronger.\n\n## Governance Tokens and DAOs\n\nA governance token refers to a blockchain-based token that grants holders the right to participate in decision-making for a protocol, typically through on-chain or off-chain votes, and in decentralized finance and Web3, governance tokens align users, developers, and investors by giving them a structured way to propose, debate, and approve changes to protocol parameters, treasury spending, and upgrades.\n\n## Governance Framework\n\nBlockchain governance can be defined as the set of rules and practices that dictate how decisions are made within a blockchain network, involving consensus mechanisms, protocol upgrades through community voting or developer proposals, and stakeholder participation including developers, miners, and users.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"c5642c59-2e17-41f3-8245-6e47ef537e7b","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:24:23.269Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"378ae35b-38c9-4ee7-abca-6772d2026e93","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

Unlike NIP-04 DMs, which expose the sender in the outer event, NIP-17 hides the sender from relays and casual observers.\n\n## Message Encryption Layers\n\nThe actual message content lives in a rumor event of kind 14. A seal encrypts that content to the recipient. A gift wrap encrypts the seal again and publishes it from a disposable keypair. The encryption algorithm MUST use the latest version of NIP-44.\n\n## NIP-59: Seals and Gift Wraps\n\nA seal is a kind:13 event that wraps a rumor with the sender's regular key. The seal is always encrypted to a receiver's pubkey but there is no p tag pointing to the receiver. There is no way to know who the rumor is for without the receiver's or the sender's private key.\n\nA gift wrap event is a kind:1059 event that wraps any other event. Tags SHOULD include any information needed to route the event to its intended recipient, including the recipient's p tag or NIP-13 proof of work.\n\n## Security Features\n\nNIP-17 offers the following privacy and security features: No Metadata Leak - Participant identities, each message's real date and time, event kinds, and other event tags are all hidden from the public. Senders and receivers cannot be linked with public information alone.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"1e8f9c8f-3b6e-4e96-8698-699012dc5b00","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:24:25.191Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"bded8262-75c2-47ae-a9f4-09f83f5d8219","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

Stripe's Machine Payments Protocol (MPP) and its specification for agent payments in 2026. Here are the key details:\n\n## Core Specification and Mechanism\n\nThe Machine Payments Protocol (MPP) is an open standard, internet-native way for agents to pay, co-authored by Tempo and Stripe. MPP provides a specification for agents and services to coordinate payments programmatically, enabling microtransactions, recurring payments, and more.\n\n## Session, Pre-funding, and Escrow Elements\n\nThe core innovation of MPP is the \"session\" mechanism, similar to OAuth in the payments domain: the Agent authorizes once and pre-deposits funds, after which each API call or data consumption is automatically settled in real time without requiring individual on-chain transactions.\n\nMPP introduces a \"sessions\" primitive that lets agents authorize a spending limit upfront and stream micropayments continuously without an on-chain transaction for each interaction.\n\n## Escrow and Settlement Model\n\nAn agent locks tokens in escrow, then streams off-chain Ed25519 signed vouchers authorizing incremental payments. The receiver settles the cumulative total onchain when ready. The sender reclaims unspent funds on close.\n\n## Launch and Technical Details\n\nMPP launched on March 18, 2026 alongside Tempo's mainnet. It was co-authored by Stripe and Tempo. This feature requires the 2026-03-04. preview API version.\n\n## Key Advantages\n\nWhere x402 requires one blockchain transaction per request, MPP introduces sessions: an agent authorizes a spending limit upfront, then streams micropayments against that session continuously without a separate on-chain transaction for each call.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"d83d81d6-f9a4-4179-b233-f57be2f3098c","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:24:39.783Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"9123f0a5-bb8e-46ac-97c4-571811aafd2d","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

The L402 protocol presents a standardized way of adding LN micropayments to any existing HTTP-REST or gRPC API.\n\n## Protocol Description\n\nThe L402 protocol is a concrete instantiation of a Lightning Network based micro-paywall for HTTP/gRPC APIs on the web. A supporting server signals that a payment is required for an endpoint by sending a special WWW-Authenticate header along with a 402 status code, which encodes an authentication token (the L402 credential), and a Lightning Network invoice.\n\n## How It Works\n\nA client requests a paid resource from a server; the server responds with 402 Payment Required, including an authentication macaroon and a Lightning invoice in the WWW-Authenticate header; the client pays the invoice over Lightning, receiving a payment preimage as proof of payment; the client re-sends the request with the macaroon and preimage in the Authorization header; and the server verifies the credential and serves the resource.\n\n## Recent Updates\n\nThe latest proposed update to the bLIP includes a version field to enable the protocol to evolve without breaking existing clients, and expands the language to be token-agnostic, using \"token\" instead of \"macaroon\" as the key name in the challenge header.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"ff95787d-dd97-411b-bbe1-15a8fb136d02","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:24:39.833Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"345b2435-5efd-4378-acb7-c91584f1a548","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

It maps Nostr public keys to human-readable internet identifiers using DNS and HTTPS, enabling verified usernames like alice@example.com.\n\nThe verification process works as follows: The client splits the identifier into local-part and domain and uses these values to make a GET request to https://<domain>/.well-known/nostr.json?name=<local-part>. The result should be a JSON document object with a key \"names\" that should then be a mapping of names to hex formatted public keys, in lowercase. If the public key for the given name matches the pubkey from the user metadata event, the client then concludes that the given pubkey can indeed be referenced by its identifier.\n\n## NIP-07: Browser Extension API for Signing\n\nNIP-07 defines window.nostr API for browser extensions to provide signing capabilities to web applications without exposing private keys.\n\n## Identity Provider Concepts\n\nThe search results reveal discussions about extending NIP-05 to support identity provider functionality. An identity provider would store your private key. You would provide proof of your identity to the identity provider (the method is not specified, for example, by entering a password). The identity provider could provide a signing tool to sign events. This opens possibility to define scopes as are known in OAuth.\n\nFor practical implementation, the Nostr WoT Extension is an all-in-one browser extension that acts as your Nostr identity provider (NIP-07 signer), Lightning wallet, and Web of Trust engine. It manages your keys in an encrypted vault, signs events for any Nostr client, handles zaps, and calculates trust scores — all from a single extension.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"dc673974-873e-4996-a92f-f18f327bd823","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:25:09.889Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"0299d001-2a56-4272-9361-943b7fbda0b5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}

System Overview and Terminology\n278\t\n279\tThe system comprises the following principal actors and components:\n280\t\n281\t**Consumer** — An end user or AI agent that invokes tools on an Operator's MCP\n282\tservice. The Consumer holds a credit balance denominated in api_sats and is\n283\tidentified by a Nostr npub.\n284\t\n285\t**Operator** — A service provider that exposes one or more tools through the Model\n286\tContext Protocol (MCP). The Operator runs the Tollbooth middleware, which gates tool\n287\taccess behind a credit balance check. The Operator holds a BTCPay Server store and\n288\ta Lightning Network node (or connection to one) for receiving payments. In the preferred embodiment, BTCPay Server is the payment processor. The OperatorRuntime abstracts payment processing behind an `ensure_btcpay()` method that constructs a payment client from vault-stored credentials, enabling future substitution of alternative Lightning-capable payment processors without changes to the credit purchase flow. The Operator\n289\tis identified by a Nostr npub and is a registered member of the DPYC Honor Chain.\n290\t\n291\t**Advocate** — A community utility service that provides shared infrastructure to\n292\tpeer MCP servers without monetization. Examples include OAuth2 callback collectors,\n293\trelay aggregators, and shared credential vaults. The Advocate is registered in the\n294\tcommunity registry with a `services[]` array that enables peer discovery via\n295\tregistry-based service name resolution. The Advocate is identified by a Nostr npub\n296\tand is a registered member of the DPYC Honor Chain, sponsored by the First Curator.\n297\t\n298\t**Authority** — A certification service that signs purchase orders for downstream\n299\tOperators.
