Let me compile the comprehensive prior art sweep report.\n\n---\n\n# Non-Patent Prior Art Sweep: Tollbooth DPYC Provisional Patent Application\n\n**Date**: April 20, 2026\n**Scope**: Open-source specifications, protocol documents, community discussions, academic papers, and production implementations\n**Invention**: Pre-funded Bitcoin Lightning micropayments for MCP tool APIs, with composable pricing constraints, Nostr-based identity, hierarchical trust chains, and AI-assisted pricing design\n\n## Claim Family Reference\n\n1. **Pre-Funded Balance Monetization** -- Consumers pre-fund api_sats via Lightning; tool invocations deduct from balance\n2. **Composable Constraint Engine** -- Pipeline of pricing constraints producing final price\n3. **Hierarchical Trust Chain** -- Authority certifies Operator purchases via Schnorr signatures; self-similar pattern\n4. **Nostr-Based Identity** -- npub as universal ID; NIP-44/NIP-17 encrypted credential exchange\n5. **Network Governance** -- GitHub-native registry under version control; economic defense\n6. **AI-Assisted Pricing Campaign Design** -- Structured AI interview co-designs pricing models\n\n---\n\n## I. BITCOIN IMPROVEMENT PROPOSALS (BIPs)\n\n### BIP-0070: Payment Protocol\n- **Source**: [BIP-0070](https://github.com/bitcoin/bips/blob/master/bip-0070.mediawiki)\n- **Date**: July 29, 2013\n- **Authors**: Gavin Andresen, Mike Hearn\n- **Relevance**: Defines merchant-customer payment communication protocol with support for micropayments (mentions disabling prompts for micropayments). However, it operates on-chain (not Lightning), uses X.509 certificates for merchant identity (not Nostr), and has no concept of pre-funded balances or constraint-based pricing. Now deprecated.\n- **Claim family**: 1 (pre-funded balance)\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** BIP-0070 is per-request payment on a different layer. No pre-funded balance, no constraint engine, no Nostr identity. Easily distinguished.\n\n### BIP-0021: URI Scheme (successor to BIP-0070)\n- **Date**: 2012\n- **Relevance**: Simple URI-based payment requests. No balance model, no API gating.\n- **Assessment**: **Not relevant** to any claim family.\n\n---\n\n## II. BOLTs (Basis of Lightning Technology)\n\n### BOLT-11: Invoice Protocol for Lightning Payments\n- **Source**: [BOLT-11 specification](https://github.com/lightning/bolts/blob/master/11-payment-encoding.md)\n- **Date**: Ongoing (part of Lightning spec since 2017)\n- **Relevance**: Defines the invoice encoding format used by the invention for credit purchase settlement. The invention uses BOLT-11 invoices as a building block. BOLT-11 itself defines invoice format only -- no balance management, no API gating, no constraint pricing.\n- **Claim family**: 1 (infrastructure the invention builds upon)\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** BOLT-11 is a component used by the invention, not prior art against any claim. It defines how invoices are encoded, not how balances are managed or APIs are gated.\n\n### BLIP-0026: L402 Lightning HTTP 402 Protocol\n- **Source**: [BLIP-0026 PR](https://github.com/lightning/blips/pull/26)\n- **Date**: Submitted ~2023, updated 2026\n- **Author**: Roasbeef (Olaoluwa Osuntokun, Lightning Labs)\n- **Relevance**: Formal specification of L402 as a Bitcoin Lightning Improvement Proposal. Defines the challenge-response flow with macaroons. Mentions caveats for attenuation (expiry, volume limits, IP binding) but these are restrictions on a single token, not a composable pricing pipeline. **No pre-funded balance, no multi-party revenue distribution, no hierarchical certification chain.**\n- **Claim family**: 1, 2\n- **Assessment**: **Closest prior art for Claim 1, but distinguishable.** L402 is per-request payment (server issues invoice per request). Token caching allows reuse but this is session authentication, not a pre-funded balance ledger. The macaroon caveat system is constraint-like but operates on access tokens, not on pricing computation. There is no balance deduction model.\n\n---\n\n## III. NIPs (Nostr Implementation Possibilities)\n\n### NIP-04: Encrypted Direct Messages\n- **Source**: [NIP-04](https://nips.nostr.com/4)\n- **Date**: 2022\n- **Relevance**: Defines AES-256-CBC encrypted DMs between Nostr keypairs. Used by the invention's Secure Courier protocol for credential exchange. NIP-04 is a building block -- it defines encryption, not a credential exchange protocol or API monetization system.\n- **Claim family**: 4\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** The invention builds upon NIP-04 as infrastructure. NIP-04 provides no API gating, no payment mechanism, no credential exchange protocol.\n\n### NIP-44: Versioned Encrypted Payloads\n- **Source**: [NIP-44](https://nips.nostr.com/44)\n- **Date**: 2023\n- **Relevance**: Improved encryption replacing NIP-04. The invention's preferred embodiment uses NIP-44 for Secure Courier. Same assessment as NIP-04 -- building block, not prior art against claims.\n- **Claim family**: 4\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.**\n\n### NIP-17: Private Direct Messages / NIP-59: Gift Wrap\n- **Source**: [NIP-17](https://nips.nostr.com/17), [NIP-59](https://nips.nostr.com/59)\n- **Date**: 2023-2024\n- **Relevance**: Defines privacy-preserving DM protocol using sealed/wrapped events with disposable keypairs. Provides stronger metadata protection than NIP-04/44. The invention could use this for credential exchange. However, NIP-17/59 define message privacy, not API monetization or credential exchange protocols.\n- **Claim family**: 4\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** Building block only.\n\n### NIP-98: HTTP Auth\n- **Source**: [NIP-98](https://nips.nostr.com/98)\n- **Date**: 2023\n- **Relevance**: Defines using Nostr events (kind 27235) to authenticate HTTP requests. The invention uses NIP-98 for authenticating pricing campaign deployment to live MCP endpoints (Claim 6). NIP-98 provides authentication, not payment gating or pricing.\n- **Claim family**: 4, 6\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** Building block for authentication. No payment, no pricing, no constraint engine.\n\n### NIP-57: Lightning Zaps\n- **Source**: [NIP-57](https://nips.nostr.com/57)\n- **Date**: 2023\n- **Relevance**: Defines tip/donation flows over Lightning via Nostr events (zap requests and receipts). Zaps are voluntary tips, not pre-funded balance purchases or API access payments. No constraint engine, no API gating.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 4\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** Zaps are social tipping, not API monetization. Easily distinguished.\n\n### NIP-47: Nostr Wallet Connect (NWC)\n- **Source**: [NIP-47](https://nips.nostr.com/47)\n- **Date**: 2023\n- **Relevance**: Defines protocol for apps to interact with Lightning wallets via Nostr relays. Supports spending limits (max_amount, budget_renewal). This is the closest Nostr-specific prior art to the balance concept -- NWC allows budget scoping. However, NWC is a wallet communication protocol, not an API monetization system. The spending limits are client-side wallet constraints, not server-side pricing constraints.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 4\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related but worth noting.** NWC's budget_renewal concept is analogous to the invention's tranche expiration, but operates at the wallet layer, not the API service layer. No constraint pipeline, no pricing engine, no trust chain.\n\n### NIP-26: Delegated Event Signing\n- **Source**: [NIP-26](https://github.com/nostr-protocol/nips/blob/master/26.md)\n- **Date**: 2022-2023\n- **Relevance**: Defines Schnorr signature-based delegation of event signing authority. Supports kind restrictions and timestamp constraints. **This is the closest NIP to the hierarchical trust chain concept.** However: (a) NIP-26 is marked \"unrecommended\" and addresses bilateral delegation only, not multi-level hierarchies; (b) it delegates signing authority, not certification of purchase orders; (c) no revenue distribution or economic model.\n- **Claim family**: 3\n- **Assessment**: **Related but distinguishable.** NIP-26 provides a mechanism for key delegation with Schnorr signatures, which is a building block. The invention's trust chain uses Schnorr-signed Nostr events for purchase order certification with fee extraction -- a fundamentally different purpose (economic certification vs. event signing delegation).\n\n### NIP-88: Recurring Subscriptions (Draft)\n- **Source**: [NIP-88 PR](https://github.com/nostr-protocol/nips/pull/866)\n- **Date**: 2023 (draft, not merged)\n- **Author**: pablof7z\n- **Relevance**: Defines recurring subscription tiers with Lightning zap-based payment verification. Includes tiered access (kind:37001 tier events) and payment receipt verification. **This is relevant to Claim 1** as it defines a payment-gated access model over Nostr.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 4\n- **Assessment**: **Related but distinguishable.** NIP-88 is a subscription model (recurring fixed payments), not a pre-funded balance model (lump-sum purchase with per-call deductions). NIP-88 has tiers but no composable constraint engine, no per-tool pricing, no hierarchical certification. It is closer to traditional subscription billing than to the invention.\n\n### NIP-ZZ: 401/402 Nostr HTTP AUTH Flow (Draft)\n- **Source**: [NIP-ZZ gist](https://gist.github.com/blakejakopovic/fe384b8fd97231ece267bf264eb466ef)\n- **Date**: May 20, 2023\n- **Author**: wakoinc\n- **Relevance**: Extends NIP-98 to define 401/402 response flows for payment-protected resources using Nostr identity. Explicitly acknowledges Lightning integration as desirable but not yet specified. **This is the most directly relevant NIP to the invention** as it combines Nostr identity with HTTP 402 payment gating.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 4\n- **Assessment**: **Related and worth careful distinction.** NIP-ZZ proposes the concept of Nostr-authenticated payment gating but explicitly states the Lightning invoice linkage is unresolved. It defines no pre-funded balance, no constraint engine, no trust chain. The invention's complete architecture is what NIP-ZZ sketched as an aspiration but never specified.\n\n---\n\n## IV. HTTP Schnorr Auth (W3C Nostr Community Group)\n\n### HTTP Authentication Using Schnorr Signatures\n- **Source**: [Spec](https://nostrcg.github.io/http-schnorr-auth/)\n- **Date**: Draft (version 0.0.1)\n- **Author/Editor**: Melvin Carvalho\n- **Relevance**: Defines Schnorr signature-based HTTP authentication aligned with Nostr identity. Uses secp256k1 BIP340 signatures in Authorization headers. No payment integration, no delegation hierarchy, no pricing.\n- **Claim family**: 4\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** Authentication building block only.\n\n---\n\n## V. MAILING LIST DISCUSSIONS\n\n### bitcoin-dev / lightning-dev Mailing Lists\n- **Source**: [bitcoin-dev Google Groups](https://groups.google.com/g/bitcoindev), [lightning-dev archives](https://www.mail-archive.com/bitcoin-dev@lists.linuxfoundation.org/maillist.html)\n- **Relevance**: Searches for \"pre-funded balance,\" \"API monetization,\" \"constraint-based pricing,\" and \"pay-per-call\" on these lists yielded no threads that describe a system combining pre-funded balances with composable constraints, trust chains, or Nostr identity. The lists contain general discussions about Lightning micropayments and L402 but nothing that anticipates the specific combination of the invention's claim families.\n- **Assessment**: **No anticipatory references found.**\n\n---\n\n## VI. GITHUB IMPLEMENTATIONS AND OPEN-SOURCE PROJECTS\n\n### L402 / Aperture (Lightning Labs)\n- **Source**: [L402 repo](https://github.com/lightninglabs/L402), [Aperture repo](https://github.com/lightninglabs/aperture)\n- **Date**: 2020 (LSAT), renamed L402 ~2023\n- **Authors**: Lightning Labs (Roasbeef, et al.)\n- **Relevance**: Aperture is a reverse proxy implementing L402. It supports: (a) fixed per-endpoint pricing in satoshis, (b) dynamic pricing via external gRPC service, (c) rate limiting via token bucket algorithm, (d) macaroon caveats for expiry/volume/IP. **Aperture's dynamic pricing and rate limiting are the closest implementation-level prior art to Claim 2 (constraint engine).**\n- **Claim family**: 1, 2\n- **Assessment**: **Significant prior art for aspects of Claims 1 and 2, but distinguishable.**\n  - **Claim 1**: Aperture is per-request payment, not pre-funded balance. A paid L402 token can be cached/reused, but there is no balance ledger, no deduction model, no tranche expiration.\n  - **Claim 2**: Aperture's dynamic pricing allows external price computation, and rate limiting is constraint-like. However, these are ad hoc configurations on a reverse proxy, not a composable pipeline of named constraint types (temporal windows, finite supply, surge, ad valorem, promotional modifiers) that are persisted as runtime-configurable pricing models with TTL-cached resolution. The invention's constraint engine is a domain-specific pipeline architecture, not a proxy configuration.\n\n### LangChainBitcoin (Lightning Labs)\n- **Source**: [GitHub](https://github.com/lightninglabs/LangChainBitcoin)\n- **Date**: July 2023\n- **Authors**: Lightning Labs\n- **Relevance**: Gives LangChain AI agents the ability to hold Bitcoin balances, send/receive Lightning payments, and traverse L402 APIs. Agents have wallet balances and spending limits via scoped macaroons.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Related but distinguishable.** The agent has a wallet balance (Lightning node balance), not a pre-funded credit balance on the service provider's ledger. The balance is on the client side; in the invention, the balance is on the server side. No constraint engine, no trust chain, no Nostr identity.\n\n### Lightning Agent Tools (Lightning Labs, February 2026)\n- **Source**: [Blog post](https://lightning.engineering/posts/2026-02-11-ln-agent-tools/)\n- **Date**: February 11, 2026\n- **Authors**: Lightning Labs\n- **Relevance**: Seven composable skills for AI agents on Lightning: pay L402 APIs, host paid endpoints, buyer/seller workflows. **Published before the invention's prior art disclosure date of Feb 17, 2026.** Mentions token caching (pay once per endpoint, not per request) and composable skills.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 2\n- **Assessment**: **IMPORTANT -- dates are close.** Published Feb 11, 2026 vs. invention's prior art disclosure Feb 16-17, 2026. However, Lightning Agent Tools still implement L402 (per-request payment with token caching), not pre-funded balances. The \"composable skills\" are agent capabilities, not pricing constraints. **Not anticipatory** of the specific claim families, but the patent attorney should carefully review the exact language in this blog post given the proximity of dates.\n\n### L402 for Agents Blog Post (Lightning Labs, March 2026)\n- **Source**: [Blog post](https://lightning.engineering/posts/2026-03-11-L402-for-agents/)\n- **Date**: March 11, 2026\n- **Authors**: Lightning Labs\n- **Relevance**: States \"an agent pays once per endpoint, not once per request\" via token caching. Mentions macaroon attenuation for spending caps, service restrictions, time-based expiration. Describes delegation where parent agents restrict child agent credentials.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 2, 3\n- **Assessment**: **Significant reference -- post-dates invention's prior art.** The \"pay once per endpoint\" with token caching is the closest L402 gets to a pre-funded model, but it is still token-based authentication, not a server-side balance ledger. Macaroon attenuation for delegation is relevant to Claim 3 but is client-side credential restriction, not server-side hierarchical certification with fee extraction. Published after Feb 17, 2026 prior art date.\n\n### Sats4AI\n- **Source**: [sats4ai.com](https://sats4ai.com), [MCP endpoint](https://sats4ai.com/mcp)\n- **Date**: Active as of April 2026\n- **Relevance**: 40+ AI tools paid via L402 Lightning micropayments. Per-request payment (agent pays invoice, gets result). No signup, no API keys, no KYC. **This is a production L402-based MCP tool marketplace.**\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Related but distinguishable.** Sats4AI is per-request L402 payment, not pre-funded balance. No constraint engine, no trust chain, no Nostr identity, no governance. Demonstrates that Lightning-gated MCP tools exist but uses a fundamentally different payment architecture.\n\n### PaidMCP (Alby)\n- **Source**: [Blog post](https://getalby.com/blog/creating-paid-mcp-servers-with-paidmcp/)\n- **Date**: July 10, 2025\n- **Relevance**: SDK for creating paid MCP servers with Lightning payments via Nostr Wallet Connect (NWC). Per-request payment model (get invoice, pay, retry). Fixed pricing per tool (e.g., \"21 sats to fetch weather data\"). No identity system, no constraint engine, no trust chain.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 4\n- **Assessment**: **Related but distinguishable.** PaidMCP uses Lightning (via NWC/Nostr) for MCP tool payment, making it the closest existing combination of Lightning + Nostr + MCP. However, it is per-request payment, not pre-funded balance. No composable constraints, no hierarchical certification, no governance. **The patent attorney should note this as it combines three of the invention's building blocks (Lightning, Nostr/NWC, MCP) but in a per-request architecture.**\n\n### PayMCP (blustAI)\n- **Source**: [GitHub](https://github.com/blustAI/paymcp), [npm](https://www.npmjs.com/package/paymcp)\n- **Date**: 2025-2026\n- **Relevance**: Provider-agnostic payment layer for MCP tools with `@price` decorator. Supports multiple payment modes including x402. Fixed pricing per tool. No Lightning support, no constraint engine, no trust chain, no Nostr identity. Uses JWT-based identity.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** Per-request payment with fixed prices. Different payment rails, different identity system, no composable constraints.\n\n### MCPay (microchipgnu)\n- **Source**: [GitHub](https://github.com/microchipgnu/MCPay)\n- **Date**: 2025-2026\n- **Relevance**: Open-source infrastructure adding x402 on-chain payments to MCP servers. Per-call USDC payments. No Lightning, no pre-funded balance, no constraints, no trust chain.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.**\n\n### xpay.sh\n- **Source**: [xpay.sh](https://www.xpay.sh/)\n- **Date**: 2025-2026\n- **Relevance**: Proxy-based MCP monetization with x402/USDC. Per-call flat-rate pricing. 5% platform fee. No Lightning, no pre-funded balance, no composable constraints.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.**\n\n### Masumi Network\n- **Source**: [masumi.network](https://www.masumi.network/)\n- **Date**: November 2024 (launch)\n- **Relevance**: Cardano-based payment protocol for AI agents with escrow smart contracts and on-chain identity. MCP integration for agent discovery. Stablecoin-based, not Lightning. No pre-funded balance model (escrow per transaction), no composable constraints, no Nostr identity.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 3\n- **Assessment**: **Related but distinguishable.** Masumi's escrow model and registry are conceptually similar to aspects of Claims 1 and 3, but uses different technology stack (Cardano vs. Lightning, on-chain identity vs. Nostr). No composable constraint engine.\n\n### Lago (Open-Source Billing)\n- **Source**: [GitHub](https://github.com/getlago/lago)\n- **Date**: 2022+\n- **Relevance**: Open-source billing platform with prepaid credit wallet functionality, usage metering, and append-only ledger. Supports \"deducting from a prepaid credit balance as usage occurs.\" **This is the closest prior art to the pre-funded balance deduction model.**\n- **Claim family**: 1, 2\n- **Assessment**: **Significant prior art for the balance deduction concept, but distinguishable.** Lago implements prepaid credits with per-usage deduction -- the same abstract pattern as Claim 1. However: (a) Lago uses traditional payment rails (Stripe/credit cards), not Lightning Network; (b) Lago is general-purpose billing infrastructure, not MCP-specific; (c) Lago has no composable constraint engine (it has pricing tiers but not a pipeline of named constraints); (d) no Nostr identity, no trust chain, no governance. **The patent attorney should ensure Claim 1 is drafted to require Lightning settlement and MCP tool invocation specifics, not just the abstract concept of prepaid credits with deduction.**\n\n### Orb Billing\n- **Source**: [withorb.com](https://www.withorb.com/)\n- **Date**: 2021+\n- **Relevance**: Billing platform with prepaid credits, custom pricing functions, and extensible pricing engine. Supports \"deducting from a prepaid credit balance as usage occurs\" with \"an append-only ledger.\" Allows custom pricing beyond standard models.\n- **Claim family**: 1, 2\n- **Assessment**: **Same assessment as Lago.** Orb has a more extensible pricing engine than Lago, but still operates in traditional payment rails with no Lightning, no MCP, no Nostr, no trust chain. Orb's \"custom pricing\" is closer to the constraint engine concept but is not described as a composable pipeline of typed constraints.\n\n---\n\n## VII. PROTOCOLS AND PLATFORMS (2025-2026)\n\n### x402 Protocol (Coinbase/Cloudflare)\n- **Source**: [x402.org](https://www.x402.org/), [Cloudflare blog](https://blog.cloudflare.com/x402/)\n- **Date**: September 2025 (launch), December 2025 (Foundation)\n- **Relevance**: HTTP 402-based payment protocol using USDC stablecoins. Two pricing schemes: \"exact\" and \"upto.\" Centralized Facilitator (Coinbase). 75M transactions / $24M by Dec 2025. MCP integration via Cloudflare Agent SDK. **Now includes deferred payment scheme.** Google integrated x402 into AP2. x402 Foundation includes Google and Visa.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Important prior art to distinguish.** x402 is the most commercially significant competing protocol. However: (a) per-request payment, not pre-funded balance; (b) only two pricing schemes (\"exact\"/\"upto\"), not a composable constraint pipeline; (c) centralized Facilitator, not decentralized trust chain; (d) stablecoins, not Lightning; (e) wallet address identity, not Nostr npub; (f) no governance mechanism. The deferred payment scheme is worth monitoring but still appears to be per-transaction, not balance-based. **Already identified and distinguished in the specification.**\n\n### Machine Payments Protocol (MPP) -- Stripe/Tempo\n- **Source**: [mpp.dev](https://mpp.dev/overview), [Stripe docs](https://docs.stripe.com/payments/machine/mpp)\n- **Date**: March 18, 2026 (launch)\n- **Authors**: Stripe + Tempo (co-authored)\n- **Relevance**: **THIS IS THE CLOSEST OVERALL PRIOR ART TO CLAIM 1.** MPP introduces a \"session\" primitive where an agent deposits funds into escrow upfront, then streams signed vouchers for subsequent requests without per-request blockchain transactions. This is conceptually similar to the pre-funded balance model. Key differences: (a) MPP uses stablecoin escrow on Tempo blockchain, not Lightning satoshi balances on a server-side ledger; (b) MPP sessions are time-limited streaming channels, not persistent balance accounts; (c) MPP supports Lightning as one payment method but the session/voucher mechanism is blockchain-based; (d) no composable constraint engine; (e) no Nostr identity; (f) no hierarchical trust chain; (g) no governance.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **CLOSEST PRIOR ART. Requires careful distinction.** MPP's session-based pre-funding is the strongest challenge to the novelty of Claim 1's pre-funded balance concept in isolation. The patent attorney must ensure claims are drafted to capture the specific combination: (a) server-side balance ledger (not on-chain escrow), (b) Lightning Network settlement (not stablecoin), (c) per-tool deduction from persistent balance (not streaming vouchers), (d) tranche-based expiration (not session close). MPP launched March 18, 2026 -- after the invention's prior art date of Feb 17, 2026 -- but the concept of pre-funded sessions may have been disclosed earlier in Stripe/Tempo discussions. **Published after prior art date but within the grace period -- investigate earlier disclosures.**\n\n### Google Agent Payments Protocol (AP2)\n- **Source**: [Google Cloud Blog](https://cloud.google.com/blog/products/ai-machine-learning/announcing-agents-to-payments-ap2-protocol), [ap2-protocol.org](https://ap2-protocol.org/)\n- **Date**: 2026\n- **Relevance**: Payment-agnostic protocol for agent payments. Integrates x402 for crypto rail. 60+ partners including Visa, Mastercard, PayPal. No pre-funded balance, no constraint engine, no Nostr identity.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** AP2 is a payment orchestration protocol, not a monetization architecture. No pre-funding, no constraints, no trust chain.\n\n### MCP Monetization Comparison Gist\n- **Source**: [GitHub Gist](https://gist.github.com/ThomsenDrake/bd5ef7f13329d6feb48e3945a23f413a)\n- **Date**: April 2026\n- **Author**: ThomsenDrake\n- **Relevance**: Directly compares four MCP monetization models: x402, L402, Tollbooth (the invention), and BTCPay invoice-per-call. Describes Tollbooth as \"prepaid tokens\" with \"asynchronous pre-funded balance\" and \"Nostr certificate chain.\" Notes Tollbooth has 199 PyPI versions (highest iteration count).\n- **Claim family**: All\n- **Assessment**: **This gist describes the invention itself** as one of four compared approaches. It confirms the invention's novelty position by contrasting it with the other three approaches (all per-request). It is evidence of the invention's public disclosure, not prior art against it.\n\n---\n\n## VIII. ACADEMIC PAPERS\n\n### \"The Internet of Value: Integrating Blockchain and Lightning Network Micropayments for Knowledge Markets\"\n- **Source**: [arXiv 2412.19384](https://arxiv.org/abs/2412.19384)\n- **Date**: December 26, 2024\n- **Authors**: Ellis Solaiman, Jorge Robins\n- **Relevance**: Proposes Lightning micropayments for Q&A knowledge markets. Conceptual framework, not implementation. No pre-funded balance, no constraint engine, no trust chain, no Nostr identity. Focuses on incentive effects of micropayments.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.** General concept of Lightning micropayments for knowledge services. No architectural overlap with the invention.\n\n### \"Enabling Micro-payments on IoT Devices using Bitcoin Lightning Network\"\n- **Source**: [arXiv 2012.10576](https://arxiv.org/abs/2012.10576), [IEEE](https://ieeexplore.ieee.org/document/9461096/)\n- **Date**: 2020\n- **Relevance**: Lightning micropayments for IoT. Different domain (IoT sensors, not API tools). No pre-funded balance model.\n- **Assessment**: **Not relevant.**\n\n### \"BitSov: A Composable Bitcoin-Native Architecture for Sovereign Internet Infrastructure\"\n- **Source**: [arXiv 2603.28727](https://arxiv.org/html/2603.28727v1)\n- **Date**: 2026\n- **Relevance**: The word \"composable\" in a Bitcoin context. Worth checking but appears to be about infrastructure sovereignty, not API pricing.\n- **Assessment**: **Likely not relevant** to claim families. Title suggests sovereignty architecture, not monetization.\n\n---\n\n## IX. BLOG POSTS AND INDUSTRY ANALYSIS\n\n### Voltage: \"Solving API Monetization Challenges with Lightning\"\n- **Source**: [Voltage blog](https://voltage.cloud/blog/solving-api-monetization-challenges-with-the-lightning-network)\n- **Date**: 2023-2024\n- **Relevance**: Describes using Lightning for API monetization via L402. Per-request model. No pre-funded balance, no constraint engine.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **Merely related.**\n\n### Orb: \"An AI Founder's Guide to Prepaid Credits\"\n- **Source**: [Orb blog](https://www.withorb.com/blog/an-ai-founders-guide-to-prepaid-credits)\n- **Date**: 2025\n- **Relevance**: Describes the prepaid credit model for AI APIs: customers buy credits upfront, credits deducted per usage. Uses traditional payment rails. **Confirms that prepaid credit models for AI APIs are a known pattern** in the industry.\n- **Claim family**: 1\n- **Assessment**: **IMPORTANT BACKGROUND.** The abstract concept of prepaid credits for API access is well-known (OpenAI, Google, etc. all use it). The invention's novelty is NOT in the concept of prepaid credits per se, but in the specific combination with Lightning settlement, composable constraints, Nostr identity, and trust chains. **The patent attorney must ensure claims are not drafted broadly enough to be anticipated by OpenAI's credit system or Lago/Orb's billing platforms.**\n\n---\n\n## X. SUMMARY OF KEY FINDINGS\n\n### Claim 1 (Pre-Funded Balance): MODERATE RISK\nThe concept of pre-funded credits with per-usage deduction is well-known (OpenAI, Lago, Orb, Google). The invention must be claimed specifically as Lightning-settled, MCP-tool-specific, with server-side balance ledger. MPP's session/escrow model is the closest technical prior art but uses different mechanisms (on-chain escrow vs. server-side ledger) and post-dates the prior art disclosure.\n\n### Claim 2 (Composable Constraint Engine): LOW RISK -- STRONGEST NOVELTY\nNo prior art found implements a composable pipeline of typed pricing constraints (temporal windows, finite supply, surge, ad valorem, promotional) that are persisted as runtime-configurable pricing models. Aperture has dynamic pricing and rate limiting but these are ad hoc proxy configurations, not a composable constraint pipeline. L402 macaroon caveats are access restrictions, not pricing computations. **This appears to be genuinely novel.**\n\n### Claim 3 (Hierarchical Trust Chain): LOW RISK -- STRONG NOVELTY\nNo prior art found implements a self-similar hierarchical trust chain where Authorities certify Operator purchase orders with Schnorr signatures and extract certification fees. NIP-26 provides Schnorr delegation but for event signing, not economic certification. X.509/TLS certificate chains are hierarchical but serve authentication, not revenue distribution. **This combination of hierarchical certification with economic fee extraction appears novel.**\n\n### Claim 4 (Nostr-Based Identity): MODERATE RISK\nUsing Nostr npub as identity for API access is emerging (PaidMCP uses NWC, NIP-98 provides HTTP auth, NIP-ZZ sketches payment gating with Nostr identity). The specific Secure Courier protocol (credential exchange via NIP-44 encrypted DMs) adds novelty. However, the building blocks are well-documented NIPs. Claims should emphasize the specific credential exchange protocol, not just \"Nostr identity for API access.\"\n\n### Claim 5 (Network Governance): LOW-MODERATE RISK\nGit-based governance registries are known in crypto (various DAO governance models). However, the specific combination of GitHub-native registry with membership verification integrated into the purchase certification flow (runtime checks during economic transactions) appears novel. No prior art found combines governance registry with payment certification.\n\n### Claim 6 (AI-Assisted Pricing Campaign Design): VERY LOW RISK -- MOST NOVEL\nNo prior art found for AI-conducted structured interviews that co-design API pricing models with constraint schema validation, multi-provider adversarial review, and cryptographically authenticated deployment. This is the most novel claim family. General AI pricing tools exist (Salesforce, Bessemer analysis) but none target MCP tool constraint pipelines with the specific methodology described.\n\n---\n\n## XI. RECOMMENDATIONS FOR PATENT ATTORNEY\n\n1. **Claim 1 must be narrowly drafted** to require Lightning Network settlement + MCP tool invocation + server-side balance ledger + tranche expiration. The abstract concept of prepaid API credits is unpatentable; the specific technical implementation is.\n\n2. **Claim 2 is the strongest independent claim.** No prior art implements composable typed pricing constraint pipelines for API monetization. Consider making this the primary independent claim.\n\n3. **Claim 3 is strong.** The self-similar trust chain with economic fee extraction via Schnorr-signed Nostr events has no close prior art.\n\n4. **Claims 4-5 are supporting claims** that strengthen the overall combination but may face more scrutiny individually.\n\n5. **Claim 6 is novel** but may face Alice/Mayo abstract idea challenges. The specification wisely ties it to specific technical processes (schema validation, NIP-98 deployment).\n\n6. **Key date concern**: Lightning Agent Tools (Feb 11, 2026) was published 5-6 days before the invention's prior art disclosure (Feb 16-17, 2026). While it describes L402 (per-request), not pre-funded balances, the proximity of dates warrants careful review.\n\n7. **MPP (March 18, 2026)**: Post-dates the prior art disclosure. Its session/escrow model is the closest architectural analog to the pre-funded balance but uses different mechanisms. Check for any earlier Stripe/Tempo disclosures of the session concept.\n\n8. **The combination is the real novelty.** No single prior art reference combines pre-funded Lightning balances + composable constraints + hierarchical trust chain + Nostr identity + governance + AI pricing design. The specification's strategy of claiming the unified system is sound."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"stop_details":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1640,"cache_read_input_tokens":72423,"output_tokens":8843,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1640},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[{"input_tokens":1,"output_tokens":8843,"cache_read_input_tokens":72423,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1640,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1640,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"type":"message"}],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CaHrmb588H4q2pekJpuWF","type":"assistant","uuid":"6fcde0ba-6ffb-4b3e-a8ac-002eb932f8a5","timestamp":"2026-04-22T00:28:35.470Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/lonniev/Development/GitHubPersonal/DPYC/dpyc-community/docs/patent","sessionId":"17bcb6af-fff6-4266-a31d-96e7a1b02dce","version":"2.1.98","gitBranch":"HEAD","slug":"abstract-cuddling-unicorn"}
